  47. Currently, we have an old standard clipper/trimmer from Wahl and a Remington cordless clipper/trimmer. These are what I will be comparing the iStubble against for this review. I've had this for approximately one month, and now that my hair has had a chance to grow back and get cut again a few times, I'm ready to do my review.<br /><br />The claim to fame for the iStubble is the lack of multiple attachments for trimming hair to different lengths, thanks to its motorized head which adjusts to the length you want at the touch of a button. The head also pivots, allowing it to be used on curved surfaces without loss of precision in cutting length. Sure, it's cordless too, but that isn't anything new.<br /><br />The iStubble comes well packaged, with multiple accessories for keeping it maintained and directions for its use. Not a whole lot of difference between what it needs and the Wahl, just a brush and some lubricating oil. Directions on usage, cleaning, and maintenance are clear and explained well. While giving it its first 16hr charge, I read over the instructions to familiarize myself with it.<br /><br />The biggest trick to using the iStubble was knowing what length I wanted and where. Typically, I know which number attachment to use for the Wahl. As far as I know, these aren't lengths, just a number. For the iStubble, I had to do a bit of conversion and thinking. I mean, just how long is .4mm anyhow? (Pretty damn short!) A bit of trial an error followed on some body areas not typically visible to others, and I had it worked out. I would not suggest you immediately start trimming your eyebrows, unless you know just how you long you want them, in metric measurement.<br /><br />True to its marketing, the iStubble worked very well when used as intended. With the guide on, no skin was pinched or accidentally cut. The shortest length of cut (.4mm) left a near smooth surface in its wake. Using the iStubble one handed was easy and fairly natural, the weight and balance just right. The lack of a cord was a boon as well, as it didn't drag all over the place while the iStubble was being used.<br /><br />I came to like the iStubble pretty quickly. While the cut it makes is narrower than the Wahl or Remington, that's a plus in several body areas. While it's not as versatile as the Wahl or Remington, both of which can be used for hairstyling/haircuts, that's quite ok with me.   76. First, the unit is well made and feels good on the hand. And it does seem to cut hair to .4 mm, which seems to be a much closer cut than the competition. In addition, the floating head feels good and, contrary to some reviewers, I had no problem shaping the stubble under the nose, though it did require some back and forth movements and, as in all razor situations, making faces. No skin irritation to report as well. Now, the not so impressive but still a tad inconsequential: the battery as shipped requires 16 hours of charge... something not competitive compared to other products that are pre-charged, or that fully chargde in an hour or two. Conair needs to address this. In this age of immediate gratification waiting nearly two days to try the device is too much. Secondly, the trimmer requires application of oil to the blades. Yet what might be something to think about is that the stubble cut by the device is, in many ways, not the \\"ideal\\" stubble grown in a day or two after a good traditional shave with a good blade (or safety blade). One explanation is that .4 mm is still not short enough for the ideal stubble if you have thick hair. I suspect something like .1 mm would be more like it. The second factor is that not all of our beard hair grows out at once... some hairs grow faster than others. The result is that a day or two \\"natural\\" stubble after a good shave will be less dense than the day after day use of the iStubble. After a few days of using the iStubble all hairs have had a chance to come out, and even if all cut at 0.4 mm they do clearly form thicker and more pronounced stubble. So, in a few words, if you have thick face hair or a lot of it your iStubble will work, but the stubble will not be that \\"ideal\\" light stubble that develops after a good shave --it will be thicker and more pronounced. Still, I am happy with the iStubble as I do not need to shave every day, and do like the stubble look more than a clean shave look. Perhaps the best out there, but, as in many things, it could be even better. ** 2013 ** Continues to go on strong, and works fine! No oiling over a year and still no problems. Once you get used to a bit thicker stubble, no complaints at all! ** 2014 ** Continues still to go on strong. Have not used it as much as in prior years, but keep it plugged in. It still holds a charge.

I left it charging for the 16 hours initially required.<br /><br />The next day is my anniversary, and I'm ready to try it out as I want to have the perfect look for my anniversary dinner. The trimmer head is a bit big and kind of painful to use around your mustache/under nose area (as many other reviewers have noted). I decided to stick with my old trimmer for this area. -1 star.<br /><br />2.) Today I went to use it and ran into a weird issue with the trimmer only allowing me to choose between .4 and 5mm. There's no in-between. I took a video of the issue: http://youtu.be/PiFJ3ELVZxk I've ordered a replacement and we'll see if this happens again. -1 star for now, but I'll happily give it back if the replacement works properly over time.<br /><br />Overall, I'm happy with my purchase and will highly recommend it if the replacement arrives and works without issue.<br /><br />Edit on 10/7/13: I received my replacement and haven't had any new issues since. Back to 4 stars.<br /><br />Update on 02/10/14: Sadly I've had to drop my review back to three stars. I think I figured out why I had that original issue - this little trimmer is VERY susceptible to moisture/water getting in to it. Basically, if I have the trimmer sitting next to my sink, and I wash my hands and shake them dry and a few drops land on the buttons of the trimmer - the water seems to just get sucked into the electronics and the device starts acting up (buttons become non-responsive). I'm not talking about immersing the device - it's literally malfunctioning just from the collateral water splash of using the sink. A huge design flaw for a device that's primarily used in a bathroom. Fortunately I've been able to keep it alive by immediately drying it out with some heat after the occasional accident, but I don't expect this to work forever.!<br /><br />I'm a new owner but I'm already in love.<br /><br />Okay, so now the bad:<br /><br />1.) However, I was under no obligation whatsoever to give it a positive review, and in fact I found some flaws.<br /><br />I don't normally grow my facial hair grow out. It's not a good look for me. But some guys can rock the perpetual five-o-clock shadow and look great doing it, and they need a better answer than simply shaving every third day. Regular clippers don't trim precisely enough to keep that stubble in the \\"sweet spot.\\"<br /><br />Enter the iStubble, which does just that, and a lot more.<br /><br />PROS<br /><br />It may like a normal electric trimmer, with a plastic guide and metal blades, but the iStubble's magic is its precision: it's adjustable in 0.2 mm increments, from 0.4 mm all the way up to 5 mm. Press the up or down buttons and the guide moves into the precise position. You don't have to guess at the correct angle in which to hold the iStubble: just press the guide flat against your face.<br /><br />The instruction sheet recommends shaving against the grain for best results, and I agree. For the neck and chin, I found it necessary to go over the area another time or two in a different direction - I later found that the instructions recommend that as well.<br /><br />If you've got more than just stubble, that 5mm setting can keep your beard, mustache or goatee from fuzzing out. I use it on my little soul patch these days - 10 seconds and I'm done.<br /><br />Because the guide folds back completely, you can use the naked blades to shape your beard or sideburns, trim your neck hairs between haircuts, and even clip stray body hairs.<br /><br />CONS<br /><br />My facial hair grows right up to within about 1/8 of an inch of my nose. Unfortunately, the iStubble's guide bumps my nose and makes it a bit of a task to trim the stubble on my upper lip. If Conair could flatten the rounded sides of the guide, the iStubble could pass under my nose with minimal contact.<br /><br />Also, the trim length resets each time I turn the iStubble on. While it's fun to watch the motorized guide move back and forth, I wish the iStubble could just remain at the last setting.<br /><br />If you're a stubble farmer, the iStubble should be your implement of choice. It's also useful even if you're clean-shaven or beardy. I'm not a big fan of non-Apple products using names that start with \\"i-\\", but this one has earned at least a pass., the trim length resets each time I turn the iStubble on.   380. The i-stubble is a quality hair trimmer with a pivoting head that does indeed conform to facial and body curves.<br /><br />Charging is easy and the LCD display gives a rough estimate of battery charge. It has a NiMH (nickel-metal hydride) battery so the first charge should be a full sixteen hours followed by three complete cycles of completely discharging the battery and recharging it to full capacity to achieve maximum battery performance. In normal use, a weekly recharge is sufficient.<br /><br />The i-stubble cuts hair to between 0.4 and 5mm with automatic adjustment of the distance from blade to comb by pushing a button with the setting displayed on the LCD screen. I didn't experience any hair pulling or pinching.<br /><br />The guide, as I said before, can't be taken off of the trimmer, but it can be flipped to the back of the trimmer, which is perfect for when trimming sideburns, etc. I didn't need to remove it when I was trimming my beard.<br /><br />Cleaning the trimmer is easy. His stubble is 0.2 to 0.3 mm ... to get that close, you need to flip back the comb head, and trim with just the metal blades against the skin - much like using [[ASIN:B000JNQSIQ Wahl Hair Clippers]] (or similar) to shave, without the guard.<br /><br />Additionally, when you flip back the head, you get a much shorter (uneven) finish, and the \\"comb\\" part is huge and bulky so you can't really get too close to the upper lip, etc. Just a clumsy design.<br /><br />The worst feature on the iStubble (design oversight) is there is no \\"catch\\" for the hair. It just jams up the cutting blades until it falls on the floor (or worse, all over your shirt). No compartment to empty. Makes a mess every time.<br /><br />But it does have it's perks - the comb head doesn't irritate the skin AT ALL. No need for soothing aftershave lotions. It's very quick, easy, and painless to use (do my whole face in say 30 seconds). But they seem to sacrifice function & versatility, and opt for cool looking design (neon glow-in-dark display, etc).<br /><br />I'd recommend the iStubble to someone with a longer goatee, who has other products for the rest of the face (i.e., if you shave with a razor, but want to keep a short or medium goatee).<br /><br />If you're looking for a all-in-one trimmer/groomer for goatee or stubble, I'd recommend something more versatile, such as ([[ASIN:B000FED5DU Norelco All-in-1 Grooming System]] (I've owned for years, and works great). No digital glow-in-the-dark display, though. But it comes with about 10 attachments for everything you need, including nose hair trimmer. For stubble, simply use it without any attachments for a perfect .2mm to .3mm stubble. The [[ASIN:B00009RF1E Wahl Groomsman Trimmer]] is similar, also for around $15, and probably just as good.<br /><br />The iStubble looks cool, and it works great for trimming chin & cheeks. But I just don't want a drawer full of electronic grooming devices. Not versatile enough for me.ompartment to empty. Overall, a great idea but some small improvements would result in a far superior product. B-

Its not suitable for longer beards (0.4mm - 5.0mm is its total range).<br />3. It doesn't collect trimmings as you shave, so could be described as a 'messy' shave.<br /><br />Its function is very simple - Its literally for achieving stubble and that's it - period, nothing more.<br /><br />Its perfect for the stubble look and can achieve stubble from 0.4mm (looks like you haven't shaved for a day) to 5.0mm...looks like you have shaved for a few weeks. Anything longer than that and you are firmly in the 'beard' category and this is not the shaver for you.<br /><br />Its cuts well and cleanly. Its mono directional pivoting head glides over the surface of the skin easily / smoothly and I find that I only need 1 - 2 passes to collect most hair. Difficult areas such as rear jaw line (between neck and ear) might need a few more passes and a shaving mirror, but this is the case for all but a few shavers that have multi-adapting / contour following, flexible heads.<br /><br />I've tried a few different types of shaver that claim to offer a genuine stubble grooming solution and this is the only one that works REALLY well. It cuts cleanly, doesn't pull / tug on hairs and is very easy to use straight out of the box. There really isn't to much to it. Switch the unit on, push up / down using the buttons on the shaver to adjust the stubble cut length (0.2mm increments, as displayed on the LCD screen) and start shaving, that's it. It is possible to remove the guard and use as a trimmer if required.<br /><br />A minor gripe would be that yes it doesn't collect your hair as you shave....but it doesn't claim to do this, so you cant really complain about it.<br /><br />The other minor thing is that you have to charge the device for 16 hours before you use it for the first time. This is so the battery is primed and will potentially have a longer life in general. Whether it does or not, I'm not really 100% sure.<br /><br />But those really are minor points...its only $38!! Which is such great value... It feels like a very well put together unit and the motor driven adjustment system works really nicely.<br /><br />If you are after a 'stubble look' and want to try out a few different lengths and styles there really is no better shaver on the market than this one at the moment.

If youdecide to buy this trimmer or any other one...Be SMART! and Keep the warranty!!!

  767. I bought this to replace a previous trimmer, looking for a closer &#34;stubble&#34; result than I was able to get from the other.<br /><br />Based on the lowest setting of my old trimmer, which that manufacturer reports as 1.6mm, I initially set the Conair to 1mm. That was a mistake. The resulting trim was MUCH shorter than I expected, almost a shave. So beware of the reported settings; they're not very accurate.<br /><br />When this trimmer is set to the same 1.6mm as my old one, it gives a MUCH closer shave. For me, it's exactly the stubble length I was looking for. My advice would be to start much higher than you think, and work down. The reported lengths are misleading. But once I arrived at the setting that works best for me, I've been very happy with the results.<br /><br />The head pivots, which does allow for a very comfortable ride as you go over the edge of your chin, etc. But I think it sometimes results in the head losing contact, and you may notice some uneven patches when you're done. Just go back over them at the same setting. Simple fix.<br /><br />Like any trimmer with a raised blade guard, it's not perfect at getting under your nose, etc. I've never found a trimmer that is.<br /><br />I think the open design of the top, where there's space between the unit and the shaving head, reduces the mess a bit. There seems to be less hair trapped in the shaver, and the flip-up head makes cleaning very easy. (Of course, you'll need to shave over the sink or in the tub/shower to avoid a mess all over the counter in any case.)<br /><br />I've noticed a few oddities with the on/off switch:<br /><br />If you press it once when you're done trimming, the blade shuts off but the unit stays powered on. You can see the battery life display and trimmer height setting. If you do nothing, it will turn off a few seconds later but &#34;remember&#34; the height setting the next time you turn the unit on. That's fine.<br /><br />But if you hold the power button down for a couple of seconds to turn the unit off manually, it will lower the blade to the lowest setting before turning off. So the next time you turn it on, it's at .4mm. If you don't notice that, your beard is gone. I find that arrangement a bit dicey.<br /><br />I've had no issues with battery life. I've used it a few times a week for several weeks and the battery is at 3/4 full. Just charge it for the full time suggested in the manual and you should be fine.<br /><br />Overall, very good trimmer at a very good price. Can't imagine you'd need your beard to be closer than this trimmer will get it.
